## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, the rate typically depends on concentration through power laws, rational functions, or more complex mechanisms, with possible explicit time dependence for driven or non-autonomous systems.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Second-order with two terms: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (mixed first and second order)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction)
- Autocatalytic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Cubic autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)**2 (higher-order autocatalytic)
- Half-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (surface-mediated or diffusion-limited)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (substrate inhibition or saturation)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (inhibition at high concentration)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-dependent rate constant)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (general polynomial mechanism)
- Fractional rational form: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (generalized saturation kinetics)
- Competing pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (sum of power-law terms)
- Exponential decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * A) (concentration-dependent activation energy analog)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no t) → autonomous ODE, likely a standard rate law: dA_dt = f(A) with power-law or rational structure
- Negative dA_dt with positive A → consumption/decay kinetics, expect negative leading coefficient
- Sign change in dA_dt at intermediate A → autocatalytic or equilibrium behavior, look for quadratic A*(c-A) forms
- Rate proportional to product of concentrations → if A0-A represents another species, expect A*(c-A) coupling terms
- Fractional power of concentration → surface reactions or diffusion-limited kinetics, A**0.5 or A**(2/3)
- Explicit time dependence → non-autonomous system, possibly photochemical or externally driven, look for t-modulated rate constants
- Rate approaching constant at high concentration → saturation kinetics, use rational forms A/(c+A)
- Multiple timescales in data → competing parallel reactions, sum of terms with different A-dependencies

- **Candidates 23, 24**: contain `A**0.5*cos(A*c)`

**Candidates 11-14, 17, 19, 22, 46, 47** have `A**0.5*c1*cos(A*c2)`. Same issue - multiplied by `sqrt(A)`.

- **Candidates 6, 8-10, 16, 23, 24, 28-30, 39-42, 44**: contain `A**c * c` terms.

**Candidate 24**: `A**0.5*c0*cos(A*c1) + A**2*c2 + A*c3 + A*c4*exp(c5*t) + A**c6*c7 + c8`

The GT has a pure `sin(cA)` term with no A-power multiplier. None of the candidates contain `sin(A*c)` directly, and `cos(A*c)` terms are always multiplied by `A**0.5` or `A**1.5`.

Could any polynomial/exponential combination approximate sin? Not exactly - we need **mathematical equivalence**, not approximation.

Let me reconsider: could `c7/(c8*exp(A*c9) + 1)` (logistic in A) match sin(cA)? No, a logistic function is monotonic, sin is oscillatory.

Could `c*exp(A*c)` terms combine to form sin? No, real exponentials can't produce oscillatory behavior.

Could `log(c*exp(A*c) + 1)` (candidate 4) produce sin? No.

After thorough analysis, **no candidate** contains a term that can produce a pure `sin(cA)` (without multiplication by a power of A). The GT fundamentally requires this term, and none of the candidates can reproduce it exactly.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.1286*sqrt(A) - 0.1286*A*exp(-0.0594*t) + 0.3894*sin(0.5829*A)`

The GT has three basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` — i.e., `A^0.5`
2. `A*exp(c*t)` — linear in A, exponential in t
3. `sin(c*A)` — a sine function of A

Key observation: The GT contains `sin(c*A)`, which is a transcendental function that cannot be exactly represented by polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, or `cos` alone (without a phase shift). Let me check which candidates have `sin` or `cos` terms that could match `sin(c*A)`.

**Candidates with `cos(A*c)` terms:** 1, 11, 12, 13, 14, 17, 19, 22, 23, 24, 43, 46, 47

Wait - let me reconsider. The candidates have terms like `A^0.5 * c1 * cos(A*c2)` or `A^1.5 * c * cos(A*c)`. The GT has `sin(c*A)` without any `A` prefactor. So:

- Candidates with `A^0.5 * cos(A*c)`: These give `A^0.5 * cos(A*c)`, not `sin(A*c)`. These are different basis functions.
- Candidates with `A^1.5 * cos(A*c)`: Similarly different.
- Candidate 23, 24: `A^0.5 * c0 * cos(A*c1)` — still `A^0.5 * cos(A*c)`, not `sin(A*c)`.

None of the candidates contain a pure `sin(c*A)` term. The `cos` terms are all multiplied by powers of A, making them fundamentally different basis functions.

**Candidates without sin/cos:** These use polynomials, exponentials, rational functions, logarithms, etc. None of these can exactly represent `sin(c*A)` for all A ≥ 0.

Let me verify each candidate systematically:

For ALL candidates: The GT requires a `sin(c*A)` term. No candidate has a bare `sin` term. The `cos` terms present are always multiplied by `A^0.5` or `A^1.5`, which makes them linearly independent from `sin(c*A)`. Polynomial, exponential, rational, and logarithmic functions cannot represent `sin(c*A)` exactly.

Therefore, **no candidate can match the GT**.
